The Four Divisions of Possible Things and Divine Attachment
Sanusi classifies possible things into four categories and resolves a dispute about divine attachment to the fourth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four categories of possible things and how divine power and will attach to each, especially the disputed fourth category, and the resolution distinguishing eligibility from actual execution.

Core Idea
Divine power attaches to all possibles, but to those that never occur it is an eligibility, not an actual execution.

Sanusi presents a classification of possible things based on their existence status. While the first three categories are straightforward, the fourth—things that will never exist—raises a question about whether divine power and will truly attach to them. The passage resolves this by distinguishing between eligibility and actual execution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four categories
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation. Notice that Sanusi lists four kinds of possible things: those that have passed, those existing now, those to come, and those that will never exist.
The fourth category is the key focus of the dispute.
2
Understand the definitive attachment for the first three
Sanusi states that power and will attach to the first three categories definitively. Reflect on why this is uncontroversial: these are things that have been, are, or will be brought into existence.
3
Examine the dispute over the fourth category
The fourth category (things that never exist) is disputed. The passage quotes a poetic explanation from Ida'at al-Dujna. Identify the two opposing views: those who affirm attachment based on original possibility, and those who deny it because knowledge of non-existence precludes it.
Some scholars seek reconciliation (tawfiq) between these views.
4
Grasp the resolution: eligibility vs. actual execution
The correct view is that attachment to the fourth category is suluhi (eligibility) not tanjizi (actual execution). Understand the difference: the power is capable in principle, but due to divine knowledge, it is not actually exercised.
This preserves both the unlimited scope of power and the consistency of divine knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملاحظة : الممكنات على أربعة أقسام ممكن وُحِدَ وانقضى وممكن موجود الآن وممكن سيوجد في المستقبل وممكن علم الله تعالى أنه لا يوجد كإيمان أبي جهل وغيره من الكفار الذين ماتوا على الكفر. وتتعلق القدرة والإرادة بكل من الأقسام الثلاثة الأولى قطعاً، وأما القسم الرابع ففيه خلاف وضّحه صاحب إضاءة الدجنة بقوله : العلم: فإن يكن علم بنفيه جرى ففي تعلق به خلف سری مثاله الإيمان من أبي لهب والبعض للتوفيق في ذاك ذهب أي من يرى تعلقاً به اعتبر إمكانه الأصلي مع قطع النظر عن غيره ومن نفاه راعى تعلق العلم به امتناعا والصحيح أن التعلق نظراً لإمكانه الأصلي، هو تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي.
Note: The possible things (mumkinat) are of four divisions: a possible that has existed and passed away; a possible that exists now; a possible that will exist in the future; and a possible that Allah knows will not exist, like the faith of Abu Jahl and other disbelievers who died upon disbelief. Power and will attach to each of the first three divisions definitively. As for the fourth division, there is a dispute about it, which the author of Ida'at al-Dujna explained by saying: Knowledge: If knowledge of its non-existence has passed, then concerning attachment to it a disagreement arose. Its example is faith from Abu Lahab. Some have sought reconciliation in that. That is, whoever sees attachment to it considers its original possibility, disregarding other considerations. And whoever denies it takes into account the attachment of knowledge to it as precluding. The correct view is that the attachment, considering its original possibility, is an attachment of eligibility (suluhi) not of actual execution (tanjizi).
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage discusses the scope of divine power and will in relation to possible things. It first categorizes possible things into four: (1) those that existed and ceased, (2) those currently existing, (3) those that will exist in the future, and (4) those that Allah knows will never exist (e.g., the faith of Abu Jahl). The first three categories are agreed upon as objects of power and will. The fourth category is disputed: can power and will attach to something that will never occur? The author cites the explanation from Ida'at al-Dujna: if knowledge has decreed its non-existence, then there is disagreement. Some hold that power and will can still be said to attach to it in terms of its original possibility (imkan asli), disregarding the knowledge of its non-occurrence. Others deny such attachment because the knowledge of its non-existence makes it impossible. The correct position is that the attachment is one of eligibility (suluhi), not actual execution (tanjizi), meaning that power and will are capable of it in principle, but due to divine knowledge they are not actually directed to it.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if Allah's power does not actually bring something into existence, then that thing is outside the scope of His power.
Correction: The passage clarifies that power can still attach to such things in terms of eligibility (suluhi), meaning it is capable of them in themselves, even if not executed due to divine knowledge.

Checkpoint

B) Eligibility (suluhi)

D) Conditional attachment

Key Takeaway
The attachment of divine power and will to possible things that never exist is one of eligibility (suluhi) not actual execution (tanjizi).

?
Consider a sin you have struggled with but feel you will never overcome. The lesson shows that even for actions Allah knows will never happen, His power 'attaches' as eligibility. How does this reshape your understanding of tawbah (repentance) and your hope in Allah's ability to change your heart? What step can you take today to act on that hope?
?

The Reality of Divine Knowledge and Its Attachment
Sanusi defines divine knowledge and explains its attachment to all things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two definitions of divine knowledge as an eternal attribute and how it attaches to all categories of knowable things.

Core Idea
Allah's knowledge is eternal, comprehensive, and attaches to all things without error.

Sanusi begins by clarifying what divine knowledge (al-ilm) is, offering two definitions that emphasize its infallibility and comprehensiveness. He then explains how this knowledge attaches to all necessary, impossible, and contingent things in an eternal actual-execution manner.

Guided Path
1
Read the two definitions
Read the Arabic passage containing the two definitions of knowledge. Notice the focus on 'disclosure without contradiction' and 'encompassing attachment without prior ignorance'.
The second definition includes a footnote marker (1) in the original.
2
Understand the attachment concept
Identify the term 'ta'allaq tanjizi qadim' (eternal actual-execution attachment). This means Allah's knowledge is eternally and actually attached to all things, not merely potential.
3
Review the examples of three categories
Read the examples for necessary, impossible, and contingent things. See how each category is known perfectly by Allah.
The examples illustrate the comprehensiveness of divine knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحقيقة العلم: صفة أزلية ينكشف بها الله كل معلوم على ما هو انكشافاً لا يحتمل النقيض بوجه من الوجوه. وقال بعضهم حقيقة العلم صفة أزلية لها تعلق بالمعلوم على وجه الإحاطة والشمول دون سبق خفاء (1). والعلم يتعلق تعلقاً تنجيزياً قديماً بجميع الواجبات والمستحيلات والجائزات، مثال الواجبات ذاته وصفاته وأسماؤه فيعلمها على الحقيقة مثال المستحيلات الزوجة والولد والشريك وسائر النقائص فيعلمها مستحيلة منفية عنه. ومثال الجائزات أنه يعلم سبحانه وتعالى جميع الجائزات ذات الممكنات وصفاتها وأسماءها ودليل العلم من الكتاب قوله تعالى {وَاللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ} [النساء : 176]، ومن السنة أنه عد في الأسماء الحسنى العليم). وقد أجمع أهل السنة على أن الله تعالى عالم بعلم. وأما برهان العقل فسيأتي.
And the reality of knowledge (al-ilm) is an eternal attribute by which Allah discloses every known thing as it is, in a disclosure that does not admit of contradiction in any respect. And some have said: The reality of knowledge is an eternal attribute that has an attachment to the known thing, in the manner of encompassing and comprehensive, without prior concealment (1). And knowledge attaches with an eternal actual-execution attachment (ta'allaq tanjizi qadim) to all necessary things (wajibat), impossible things (mustahilat), and contingent things (ja'izat). Example of necessary things: His essence, attributes, and names—He knows them in reality. Example of impossible things: spouse, child, partner, and all deficiencies—He knows them as impossible and negated from Him. Example of contingent things: He, glorified and exalted, knows all contingent things, the essences of possible things, their attributes and names. And the proof of knowledge from the Book is His saying: 'And Allah is of all things Knowing' (al-Nisa 4:176). And from the Sunna is that He enumerated 'al-Alim' among the beautiful names. And the people of the Sunna have consensus that Allah Almighty is knowing (alim) by knowledge. As for the rational proof, it will come later.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of knowledge (al-ilm) as an eternal attribute that allows Allah to know all things infallibly. Two definitions are given: the first emphasizes disclosure without possibility of error; the second emphasizes comprehensive attachment without prior ignorance. Then it explains that knowledge attaches (ta'allaq tanjizi) to all three categories: necessary (wajibat), impossible (mustahilat), and contingent (ja'izat), giving examples for each. Finally, it provides textual evidence from the Qur'an and Sunna, and consensus, that Allah is knowing by knowledge, noting that rational proof will follow.

التعلق التنجيزي

الجائزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah's knowledge is acquired or learned over time.
Correction: Allah's knowledge is eternal and does not involve prior ignorance; it is an eternal attachment.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what kind of attachment does knowledge have to all things?
A) Potential attachment (suluhi)
B) Actual-execution attachment (tanjizi)
C) Attachment after concealment
D) No attachment

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge is an eternal attribute that perfectly and comprehensively attaches to all things without error or prior ignorance.

Scriptural Proofs for Divine Knowledge
Sanusi provides scriptural proof for divine knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence for Allah's attribute of knowledge from the Qur'an, Sunna, and consensus of Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
The Qur'an, Sunna, and Ijma all testify that Allah is Knowing by an eternal knowledge.

After defining divine knowledge, Sanusi provides the scriptural evidence. He cites a Qur'anic verse, mentions the beautiful name al-Alim from the Sunna, and notes the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna. The rational proof is deferred to later discussion.

2
Note the Sunna and Ijma
Sanusi then cites the name 'al-Alim' from the beautiful names (al-asma' al-husna) and the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna that Allah is knowing by knowledge.
Consensus (ijma) is a major source of proof in theology.
3
Observe the deferral
Notice that rational proof is mentioned but postponed. This highlights that textual evidence suffices at this stage.

The Four Divisions of Possibles and the Disagreement on the Fourth
Classifies possibles into four divisions and discusses the disagreement on the fourth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four divisions of possible things and the disagreement about God's power and will attaching to the fourth division, as well as the correct position of potential attachment.

Core Idea
God's power and will attach to all possibles, but only potentially to the fourth.

In this passage, the author classifies possible things into four categories based on their existence status. He then explains that there is unanimous agreement that God's power and will attach to the first three categories, but there is a dispute regarding the fourth—the things God knows will never exist. The correct view distinguishes between potential and actual attachment.

Guided Path
1
Learn the four divisions
The passage lists four types of possibles: past, present, future, and never-existing. Read the Arabic and translation to understand each.
2
Understand the agreement on the first three
The passage states that power and will attach definitively to the first three. Note that this is unanimous.
3
Study the disagreement on the fourth
The author quotes a poem explaining the dispute. Some consider attachment based on original possibility, others deny it based on God's knowledge of non-existence.
4
Grasp the correct view
The passage concludes that attachment to the fourth is potential (ṣulūḥī), not actual (tanzīzī). This resolves the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ملاحظة : الممكنات على أربعة أقسام ممكن وُحِدَ وانقضى وممكن موجود الآن وممكن سيوجد في المستقبل وممكن علم الله تعالى أنه لا يوجد كإيمان أبي جهل وغيره من الكفار الذين ماتوا على الكفر. وتتعلق القدرة والإرادة بكل من الأقسام الثلاثة الأولى قطعاً، وأما القسم الرابع ففيه خلاف وضّحه صاحب إضاءة الدجنة بقوله :
فإن يكن علم بنفيه جرى ففي تعلق به خلف سری مثاله الإيمان من أبي لهب والبعض للتوفيق في ذاك ذهب أي من يرى تعلقاً به اعتبر إمكانه الأصلي مع قطع النظر عن غيره ومن نفاه راعى تعلق العلم به امتناعا
والصحيح أن التعلق نظراً لإمكانه الأصلي، هو تعلق صلوحي لا تنجيزي.
Note: Possibles are of four divisions: a possible that has existed and passed away, a possible that exists now, a possible that will exist in the future, and a possible that God the Exalted knows will not exist, like the faith of Abu Jahl and other disbelievers who died upon disbelief. And power and will attach definitively to each of the first three divisions. As for the fourth division, there is a disagreement concerning it, which the author of Iḍāʾat al-Dujnah clarified by his saying: 'If knowledge has occurred concerning its non-existence, then concerning attachment to it there is a hidden disagreement; its example is the faith of Abu Lahab, and some went to reconciliation in that.' That is, whoever sees attachment to it considers its original possibility without consideration of other factors; and whoever denies it considers the attachment of knowledge to it an impossibility. And the correct view is that attachment, in view of its original possibility, is a potential (ṣulūḥī) attachment, not an actual (tanzīzī) one.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage classifies possible things (mumkināt) into four types and then discusses the disagreement regarding the attachment (tawalluq) of power (qudra) and will (irāda) to the fourth type. It begins by enumerating: (1) a possible that has existed and passed, (2) a possible existing now, (3) a possible that will exist in the future, (4) a possible that God knows will never exist, such as the faith of Abu Jahl and similar disbelievers who died in disbelief. The passage states definitively that power and will attach to the first three types. As for the fourth, there is a disagreement, clarified by the author of Iḍāʾat al-Dujnah in his poem. The poem states: if knowledge (ʿilm) has occurred concerning its non-existence, then there is a dispute about attachment to it. The example is the faith of Abū Lahab. Some consider attachment, taking into account its original possibility (imkānuhu al-aṣlī) disregarding other factors; others deny it, considering that knowledge of its non-existence precludes it. The correct view, according to the text, is that the attachment, in view of its original possibility, is a potential (ṣulūḥī) attachment, not an actual (tanzīzī) one. That is, the power and will are capable of attaching to it in principle but do not do so because God knows it will never be.

Key Terms
ممكن
قسم رابع
تعلق صلوحي
تعلق تنجيزي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's power and will attach to all possible things in an actual sense, including those that will never exist.
Correction: In fact, for things that God knows will never exist, the attachment of power and will is only potential (ṣulūḥī), not actual (tanzīzī).

Checkpoint

C) A possible that will exist in the future.

Key Takeaway
The fourth division of possibles (things God knows will never exist) receives only a potential attachment of power and will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The correct view says attachment is potential, not actual. This means God's power is capable regarding what He knows will not happen, but He does not bring it about. The Attribute of Knowledge: Definition, Attachment, and Proofs
Defines the attribute of knowledge and explains its three types of attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the divine attribute of knowledge, its three types of attachment, and the scriptural proofs for it.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is eternal, actual, and encompasses all things.

This passage introduces one of the essential divine attributes: knowledge. It provides a precise definition, explains how God's knowledge relates to all categories of things, and offers scriptural evidence. By studying this, you gain a foundation for understanding how Islamic theology affirms God's omniscience.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own phrasing come through before interpreting.
2
Identify the two definitions of knowledge
The passage gives two definitions. Notice how the second definition adds the idea of 'comprehensive attachment without prior concealment'.
3
Examine the three types of attachment
Knowledge attaches actually and eternally to necessary, impossible, and contingent things. Find examples for each category in the passage.
4
Review the scriptural and consensus proofs
The passage cites a Qur'anic verse, the Sunnah, and consensus. Note how these establish the attribute of knowledge.
5
Understand the note about actual vs potential attachment
The note clarifies that all attachment is actual and eternal, rejecting potential attachment. Reflect on why this matters for God's omniscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحقيقة العلم: صفة أزلية ينكشف بها الله كل معلوم على ما هو انكشافاً لا يحتمل النقيض بوجه من الوجوه. وقال بعضهم حقيقة العلم صفة أزلية لها تعلق بالمعلوم على وجه الإحاطة والشمول دون سبق خفاء. والعلم يتعلق تعلقاً تنجيزياً قديماً بجميع الواجبات والمستحيلات والجائزات، مثال الواجبات ذاته وصفاته وأسماؤه فيعلمها على الحقيقة مثال المستحيلات الزوجة والولد والشريك وسائر النقائص فيعلمها مستحيلة منفية عنه. ومثال الجائزات أنه يعلم سبحانه وتعالى جميع الجائزات ذات الممكنات وصفاتها وأسماءها ودليل العلم من الكتاب قوله تعالى ( وَاللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ ) (النساء : ١٧٦]، ومن السنة أنه عد في الأسماء الحسنى العليم) . وقد أجمع أهل السنة على أن الله تعالى عالم بعلم. وأما برهان العقل فسيأتي.
ملاحظة : تعلق العلم كله تنجيزي قديم وليس له تعلق صلوحي لأن من صلح لأن يعلم فليس بعالم في الحال.
And the reality of knowledge: it is an eternal attribute by which God discloses every known thing as it is, with a disclosure that does not admit the opposite in any way. And some said: the reality of knowledge is an eternal attribute that has an attachment to the known object in a comprehensive and inclusive manner without prior concealment. And knowledge attaches in an actual eternal attachment to all necessary things, impossible things, and contingent things. Example of necessary things: His essence, attributes, and names – He knows them in reality. Example of impossible things: spouse, child, partner, and all deficiencies – He knows them as impossible and negated from Him. Example of contingent things: He, glorified and exalted, knows all contingent things, the essences of possibles, their attributes and names. The proof of knowledge from the Book is His saying 'And Allah is of all things Knowing' (Qur'an 4:176), and from the Sunnah that it is counted among the Beautiful Names: 'the Knowing'. And the people of the Sunnah have unanimously agreed that God the Exalted is knowing with a knowledge. As for the intellectual proof, it will come later. Note: The attachment of knowledge is all actual and eternal; there is no potential attachment for it, because one who is fit to know is not actually knowing in the present.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of knowledge (al-ʿilm) and describes its attachment to all categories. It begins with two definitions: first, knowledge is an eternal attribute (ṣifa azaliyya) by which God discloses every known thing as it is, with a disclosure that admits no opposite in any way. Second, an alternative definition given by some is: an eternal attribute that has a relation to the known object in a comprehensive and inclusive manner without prior concealment. The passage then explains that knowledge attaches in an actual eternal attachment (tawalluq tanzīzī qadīm) to all necessary things (wājibāt), impossible things (mustaḥīlāt), and contingent things (jāʾizāt). Examples of necessary things are God's essence, attributes, and names; He knows them in reality. Examples of impossible things are spouse, child, partner, and all deficiencies; He knows them as impossible and negated from Him. Examples of contingent things are all possible things, their attributes and names. The scriptural proof from the Qur'an is 'And Allah is of all things Knowing' (4:176). From the Sunnah, the name 'al-ʿAlīm' is among the Beautiful Names. The Sunni community unanimously agrees that God is knowing with a knowledge. The intellectual proof will come later. The passage ends with a note: all attachment of knowledge is actual and eternal; there is no potential attachment, because one who could potentially know is not actually knowing in the present.

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is an eternal attribute that actually encompasses all necessary, impossible, and contingent things, as affirmed by scripture and consensus.

?

?
The passage says God knows all impossible things—things that cannot happen. If you truly believed that nothing escapes His knowledge, what worry or anxiety would you let go of right now? Take a moment to name it and entrust it to His all-encompassing awareness.
?
God knows you completely—your weaknesses, failures, and sins. Yet He still calls you to turn to Him. How does this knowledge affect your view of yourself? Will you stop hiding from His gaze and instead seek His mercy today?

The Attribute of Life: Definition, Condition, and Proofs
Defines life as a condition for perception and provides proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the attribute of life as an eternal condition for perception, its distinction from other divine attributes, and the scriptural evidence for it.

Core Idea
Life is not an active attribute but a condition for perception.

In this passage, Sanusi explains the divine attribute of life (al-ḥayāh). He defines it as an eternal attribute that enables its possessor to have perception, clarifies that it functions as a rational condition rather than an active cause, and distinguishes it from attributes of effect, disclosure, and indication. Finally, he cites scriptural proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, along with consensus.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of life
Read the first sentence defining life as an eternal attribute that qualifies for perception. Note that perception here includes hearing, sight, and knowledge.
2
Grasp life as a condition
Read how life is a rational condition (sharṭ ʿaqlī) for the attributes of meanings. Its absence prevents perception, but its presence does not guarantee it.
3
Distinguish life from other attributes
Notice the clarification that life does not attach to anything; it is not like power, will (effect), hearing, sight, knowledge (disclosure), or speech (indication).
4
Review the scriptural proofs
Examine the Quranic verse (25:58) and the prophetic supplication. Understand that these are essential proofs for the necessity of life.
5
Recognize the consensus
See that the ummah unanimously agrees that God is living with a life. The intellectual proof is deferred to later.

وحقيقة الحياة صفة أزلية تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك. والمراد بصفات الإدراك السمع والبصر والعلم ولا مفهوم للإدراك. فالحياة شرط عقلي في صفات المعاني يلزم من عدمها عدم الإدراك ولا يلزم من وجودها وجود الإدراك ولا عدمه. فالإدراك واجب الله لقيام الأدلة على ذلك. والحياة لا تتعلق بشيء، وإنما هي شرط في جميع صفات المعاني ومن صفة نفسها أنها لا تتعلق بشيء، أي لا تطلب أمراً زائداً على قيامها بمحلها فليست من صفات التأثير كالقدرة والإرادة ولا من صفات الانكشاف كالسمع والبصر والعلم، ولا من صفات الدلالة كالكلام. والدليل على وجوب الحياة من الكتاب قوله تعالى ( وَتَوَكَّلْ عَلَى الْحَى الَّذِى لا يَمُوتُ ) [الفرقان: ۱۵۸]، ومن السنة قوله : 'اللهم يا حي يا قيوم' . وقد أجمعت الأمة على أن الله تعالى حي بحياة. وبرهان العقل فسيأتي.
And the reality of life: an eternal attribute that qualifies its bearer to be described with the attributes of perception. And what is meant by attributes of perception are hearing, sight, and knowledge; there is no concept for perception itself. Life is a rational condition for the attributes of meanings; its absence necessitates the absence of perception, but its existence does not necessitate the existence or absence of perception. Perception is obligatory for God due to the proofs established for that. And life does not attach to anything; rather it is only a condition for all attributes of meanings, and from its own description is that it does not attach to anything, meaning it does not require anything beyond its subsistence in its locus. So it is not among the attributes of effect like power and will, nor among the attributes of disclosure like hearing, sight, and knowledge, nor among the attributes of indication like speech. The proof for the necessity of life from the Book is His saying 'And rely upon the Ever-Living who does not die' (Qur'an 25:58), and from the Sunnah, his saying: 'O Allah, O Ever-Living, O Self-Sustaining.' And the community has unanimously agreed that God the Exalted is living with a life. The intellectual proof will come later.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of life (al-ḥayāh) and explains its role as a condition for perception. It begins by defining life as an eternal attribute that qualifies its bearer to be described with attributes of perception (idrāk). The attributes of perception are hearing, sight, and knowledge; perception itself has no independent concept. Life is a rational condition (sharṭ ʿaqlī) for the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī); its absence entails absence of perception, but its presence does not necessarily entail presence or absence of perception—perception is obligatory for God due to other proofs. The passage then clarifies that life does not attach to anything; it is only a condition for all attributes of meanings. Unlike power (qudra) and will (irāda) which are attributes of effect, or hearing, sight, and knowledge which are attributes of disclosure (inkishāf), or speech which is an attribute of indication (dalāla), life has no requirement beyond subsisting in its locus. The scriptural proof from the Qur'an is 'And rely upon the Ever-Living who does not die' (25:58). From the Sunnah, the supplication 'O Allah, O Ever-Living, O Self-Sustaining.' The community unanimously agrees that God is living with a life. The intellectual proof will come later.

Correction: Life is a condition, not an active cause; it is necessary for perception but does not itself bring about anything beyond subsistence in its locus.

?

Will you consciously acknowledge this dependence in your next action, saying inwardly, 'I can only do this because He keeps me alive'?

The Divine Attribute of Life: Definition and Role
Definition and textual proof for the attribute of Life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the divine attribute of Life, its role as a condition for the attributes of perception, and the evidence for its necessity.

Core Idea
Life is not an active attribute; it is a precondition for perception.

In this passage, Imam Sanusi defines the attribute of Life (al-Ḥayāh) and clarifies its function. He explains that Life is an eternal attribute that makes it possible for Allah to have perception, but it does not itself produce perception. This distinction is crucial for understanding the nature of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the opening sentence defining Life as an eternal attribute that qualifies for perception.
Pay attention to the phrase 'eternal attribute' (ṣifa azaliyya).
2
Understand Life as a condition
Notice that Life is a condition (sharṭ) for perception: its absence prevents it, but its presence does not guarantee perception.
This is the key logical point: Life is necessary but not sufficient.
3
Distinguish from other attributes
Life does not relate to anything external; it is not an attribute of effect, disclosure, or indication.
Compare with Power, Will, Hearing, Sight, Knowledge, and Speech.
4
Review the proofs
Examine the textual evidence: Quran (25:58), Sunnah (prophetic supplication), and consensus.
The intellectual proof is deferred to a later discussion.
5
Check your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm your grasp of Life's role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحياة
وحقيقة الحياة صفة أزلية تصحح لمن قامت به أن يتصف بصفات الإدراك. والمراد بصفات الإدراك السمع والبصر والعلم ولا مفهوم للإدراك. فالحياة شرط عقلي في صفات المعاني يلزم من عدمها عدم الإدراك ولا يلزم من وجودها وجود الإدراك ولا عدمه. فالإدراك واجب الله لقيام الأدلة على ذلك.
والحياة لا تتعلق بشيء، وإنما هي شرط في جميع صفات المعاني ومن صفة نفسها أنها لا تتعلق بشيء، أي لا تطلب أمراً زائداً على قيامها بمحلها فليست من صفات التأثير كالقدرة والإرادة ولا من صفات الانكشاف كالسمع والبصر والعلم، ولا من صفات الدلالة كالكلام.
والدليل على وجوب الحياة من الكتاب قوله تعالى (وَتَوَكَّلْ عَلَى الْحَى الَّذِى لا يَمُوتُ) [الفرقان: 158]، ومن السنة قوله: "اللهم يا حي يا قيوم". وقد أجمعت الأمة على أن الله تعالى حي بحياة. وبرهان العقل فسيأتي.
Life: The reality of Life is an eternal attribute that makes it correct for the one described by it to be described with the attributes of perception. What is meant by the attributes of perception are Hearing, Sight, and Knowledge, and perception has no distinct meaning. So Life is an intellectual condition in the attributes of meanings; its absence necessitates the absence of perception, but its existence neither necessitates perception nor its absence. Perception is necessary for Allah due to the establishment of evidences for that. Life does not relate to anything; rather it is a condition in all the attributes of meanings, and from its own description it does not relate to anything, meaning it does not require something additional beyond its subsistence in its locus. Thus it is not among the attributes of effect like Power and Will, nor among the attributes of disclosure like Hearing, Sight, and Knowledge, nor among the attributes of indication like Speech. The textual proof for the necessity of Life is from the Book: His saying Exalted is He: 'And rely upon the Alive who does not die' [Al-Furqan: 158], and from the Sunnah: his saying (peace be upon him): 'O Allah, O Living, O Self-Subsisting.' And the community has unanimously agreed that Allah Exalted is He is Living with a Life. The intellectual proof will come later.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of Life (al-Ḥayāh) and provides scriptural proof. It begins by stating the definition: Life is an eternal attribute that qualifies its possessor to have attributes of perception—specifically Hearing, Sight, and Knowledge. Perception itself has no separate meaning beyond these three; it is merely a label for them. The author then explains that Life is an intellectual condition (sharṭ ʿaqlī) for these attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī): if Life is absent, perception is impossible, but if Life is present, perception may or may not exist—it does not guarantee it. Perception is necessary for Allah because evidence (Qur’an, Sunnah, consensus) proves He perceives. The passage clarifies that Life does not relate to anything external; it does not require an object beyond itself. Unlike attributes of effect (Power, Will) which require objects, or disclosure attributes (Hearing, Sight, Knowledge) which require things to be disclosed, or indication attributes (Speech) which require meaning, Life is merely a condition for other attributes. The proof is from the Qur’anic verse 'And rely upon the Alive who does not die' (25:58), the Prophet’s supplication 'O Allah, O Living, O Self-Subsisting', and the consensus of the Muslim community that Allah is living with a Life. The intellectual proof is deferred to a later discussion.

Correction: Life is merely a condition (sharṭ) for perception; it does not produce effects or relate to anything external.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
Life is a precondition for perception. If you seek to know Allah through His attributes of Knowledge, Hearing, and Sight, but ignore the precondition of Life, aren't you treating Him as a dead concept? What step will you take this week to engage with Allah as the Living One, not a set of ideas?

The Divine Attributes of Hearing and Sight
Definition and proof of Allah's Hearing and Sight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of Allah's attributes of Hearing and Sight, their distinctness from knowledge, and their modes of relation to eternal and temporal existents.

Core Idea
Allah's Hearing and Sight are eternal attributes with distinct disclosures, not reducible to knowledge.

This passage from the Sharḥ al-Sanūsiyyah explains two of Allah's essential attributes: Hearing (al-Samʿ) and Sight (al-Baṣar). The author defines their reality, clarifies they are distinct from each other and from divine knowledge, and details how they relate to all existents—both eternal and temporal. A scriptural proof is also provided.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own words set the stage.
The passage uses technical terms like 'inkishāf' and 'taʿalluq'.
2
Understand the definition
Identify that Hearing and Sight are defined as eternal attributes (ṣifa azaliyya) by which every existent is disclosed to Allah.
Note that 'eternal' means they are not created or temporal.
3
Distinguish the disclosure
Notice the author stresses that the disclosure of Hearing is different from the disclosure of Sight, emphasizing they are two distinct attributes.
This guards against thinking they are identical to each other or to knowledge.
4
Analyze the relation to existents
Break down the two types of relation (taʿalluq): tanzīzī (immediate) and ṣulūḥī (potential), and how they apply to eternal vs. temporal objects.
The relation to Allah's essence and attributes is tanzīzī qadīm; to contingent beings it is tanzīzī ḥādith and ṣulūḥī qadīm.
5
Reflect on the proof
Read the Quranic proof: 'And He is the Hearing, the Seeing.' Consider why this verse is sufficient as evidence.
The proof is scriptural (naqlī), not rational, but the attributes are rationally necessary as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمع والبصر:
وحقيقة كل من السمع والبصر صفة أزلية ينكشف بها لله كل موجود. وانكشاف السمع يباين انكشاف البصر.
وهما صفتان كما ورد النقل بهما ووجب الإيمان بهما ولا يزيدان على علمه في الانكشاف بل في حقيقتهما وتعلقهما الخاص بهما وهو تعلقهما بالموجودات سواء كانت الموجودات قديمة كذاته العلية وجميع صفاته الموجودة، أو حادثة كذوات الكائنات وجميع صفاتها الوجودية. وتعلقهما بذاته وصفاته الوجودية تنجيزي قديم، وبذوات الكائنات وصفاتها الوجودية تنجيزي حادث وصلوحي قديم.
والدليل على وجوب السمع والبصر من الكتاب قوله تعالى: (وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ).
Hearing and Sight: The reality of each of Hearing and Sight is an eternal attribute by which every existent is disclosed to Allah. The disclosure of Hearing is different from the disclosure of Sight. They are two attributes, as transmitted proof has come concerning them and faith in them is obligatory. They do not increase upon His knowledge in disclosure, but rather in their reality and their special relation, which is their relation to existents, whether the existents are eternal like His sublime Essence and all His existing attributes, or temporal like the essences of contingent beings and all their existential attributes. Their relation to His Essence and His existential attributes is an immediate pre-eternal relation, and to the essences of contingent beings and their existential attributes it is an immediate temporal relation and a potential pre-eternal relation. The proof for the necessity of Hearing and Sight from the Book is His saying Exalted is He: 'And He is the Hearing, the Seeing.'
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attributes of Hearing (al-Samʿ) and Sight (al-Baṣar) and provides scriptural proof. It begins by stating the definition: each is an eternal attribute by which every existent is disclosed to Allah. Although both disclose, the mode of disclosure differs—Hearing's disclosure is distinct from Sight's. The author asserts that these are two distinct attributes; transmitted evidence necessitates belief in them. They do not add to God's knowledge in terms of disclosure—meaning they do not reveal more than what His knowledge already encompasses—but they are distinct in their reality and in their special relation to objects. Their relation covers all existents: eternal (God's essence and attributes) and temporal (contingent beings and their attributes). For eternal objects, the relation is immediate (tanzīzī) and pre-eternal (qadīm); for temporal objects, the relation is immediate and temporal (ḥādith) but also potential (ṣulūḥī) and pre-eternal. The proof from the Quran is the verse: 'And He is the Hearing, the Seeing.'

البصر

الانكشاف
التعلق التنجيزي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Hearing and Sight are identical to God's knowledge or that they imply physical organs.
Correction: The author emphasizes they are distinct attributes with special relations, not reducible to knowledge. They are eternal, non-physical attributes of disclosure.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Allah's Hearing and Sight are real, distinct eternal attributes that disclose all existents, with specific relations to eternal and temporal beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Definition and Nature of Hearing and Sight
Defines hearing and sight as attributes of disclosure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of hearing and sight as eternal attributes of disclosure, their distinct reality, and their relation to different types of existents.

Core Idea
Hearing and sight disclose all things without being identical to knowledge.

Sanusi begins by defining hearing and sight as eternal attributes through which every existent is disclosed to God. He emphasizes that they are two distinct attributes, not reducible to knowledge, and explains how they relate to God's essence and attributes on one hand and to contingent beings on the other. This sets the conceptual foundation before moving to proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the opening sentence carefully: 'The reality of each of hearing and sight is an eternal attribute by which every existing thing is disclosed to God.' Note the phrase 'eternal attribute' and 'disclosed.'
This definition establishes that these attributes are not acquired or created.
2
Distinguish hearing and sight
Notice that the author states the disclosure of hearing is distinct from that of sight, though both disclose. Consider why this distinction matters—it shows they are not redundant.
They are two separate attributes with different modes of disclosure.
3
Understand their relation to existents
The passage explains the relation (ta‘alluq) to eternal things (God’s essence and attributes) and originated things (contingent beings). For eternal things, the relation is active and eternal; for originated things, it is active and originated but also potential and eternal.
This complex relation helps avoid temporal change in God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمع والبصر : وحقيقة كل من السمع والبصر صفة أزلية ينكشف بها لله كل موجود. وانكشاف السمع يباين انكشاف البصر. وهما صفتان كما ورد النقل بهما ووجب الإيمان بهما ولا يزيدان على علمه في الانكشاف بل في حقيقتهما وتعلقهما الخاص بهما وهو تعلقهما بالموجودات سواء كانت الموجودات قديمة كذاته العلية وجميع صفاته الموجودة، أو حادثة كذوات الكائنات وجميع صفاتها الوجودية. وتعلقهما بذاته وصفاته الوجودية تنجيزي قديم، وبذوات الكائنات وصفاتها الوجودية تنجيزي حادث وصلوحي قديم. والدليل على وجوب السمع والبصر من الكتاب قوله تعالى : ( وَهُوَ السَّمِيعُ الْبَصِيرُ ) لا إله إلا أنت بديع السماوات والأرض يا ذا الجلال والإكرام يا حي يا قيوم فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لقد دعا باسم الله الأعظم الذي إذا دعي به أجاب وإذا سئل به أعطى . هذا حديث صحيح على شرط مسلم ولم يخرجاه وقد روي من وجه آخر عن أنس بن مالك. ورواه النسائي في المجتبى عن أنس أيضاً. وهذا الدعاء "يا حي يا قيوم" كان الرسول عليه السلام يكثر من استعماله ، كما رواه أصحاب السنن ، فقد روى الحاكم والنسائي في السنن الكبرى عن علي رضي الله عنه ، أن الرسول عليه السلام دعا به في غزوة بدر. وهذا اللفظ مشهور في ذلك الأحاديث. (س). (۱) فيسمع سبحانه ويرى في الأزل ذاته العلية وجميع صفاته الوجودية التي منها سمعه وبصره ويسمع ويرى مع فيما لا يزال ذوات الكائنات كلها وجميع صفاتها الوجودية كيف ما كان كل منهما، فسمعه تعالى وبصره ليس بشرط عدم البعد جداً وعدم السر جداً وبصرنا إنما يتعلق عادة ببعض الموجودات وهو الأجسام وألوانها وحركتها وسكونها بشرط أن يكون المرئي في جهة الأمام وأن لا يكون بعيداً جداً ولا قريباً جداً .(غ) وهذا لأن سمعه تعالى صفة من صفاته، وليس عضواً منه كما يتوهم المجسمة، فيقولون إن الله عينين وإن كل عين منهما يشار إليها إشارة غير ما يشار إلى الأخرى، وأن إحداهما على يمين الأخرى، فهذا تجسيم محض ، تعالى الله عنه، وهو من افتراءات المجسمة. وأما نحن فنقول كما أن الله صفة هي العلم فله أيضاً صفة هي السمع وسمعه بلا عضو ولا جارحة، كما هو في المخلوق، وكذا يقال في بصره. (س). السنة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما مرَّ بأناس يستسقون ويدعون الله جهراً فقال : "يا أيها الناس أربعوا على أنفسكم - أي أمهلوا عليها - فإنكم لم تدعوا أصم ولا أعمى وإنما تدعون سميعاً بصيراً (۱) . وأجمعت الأمة على أن الله تعالى سميع بصير، ودليل العقل فسيأتي. ملاحظة : اعلم أنه تعالى يسمع سمعه بسمعه ويبصر بصره ببصره كما أنه يعلم علمه بعلمه، لأن صفات الانكشاف تتعلق بأنفسها بخلاف صفات التأثير فإنها تتعلق بالممكنات فقط.
Hearing and sight: The reality of each of hearing and sight is an eternal attribute by which every existing thing is disclosed to God. The disclosure of hearing is distinct from the disclosure of sight. They are two attributes as transmitted reports have come about them and faith in them is obligatory. They do not increase over His knowledge in disclosure, but rather in their reality and their specific relation, which is their relation to existents, whether the existents are eternal like His high essence and all His existing attributes, or originated like the essences of contingent things and all their existential attributes. Their relation to His essence and His existential attributes is an eternal active relation, and to the essences of contingent things and their existential attributes it is an originated active relation and an eternal potential relation. The proof for the necessity of hearing and sight from the Book is His statement exalted: 'And He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing.' There is no god but You, the originator of the heavens and the earth, O Possessor of majesty and honor, O Living, O Self-Subsisting, so the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'He has called upon the greatest name of God, which when invoked thereby He answers, and when asked thereby He gives.' This hadith is authentic on the condition of Muslim, but they did not record it, and it has been narrated from another chain from Anas ibn Malik. Al-Nasa'i also narrated it in al-Mujtaba from Anas. And this supplication 'O Living, O Self-Subsisting' the Messenger (peace be upon him) used frequently, as narrated by the authors of the Sunan. Al-Hakim and al-Nasa'i in al-Sunan al-Kubra narrated from Ali (may God be pleased with him) that the Messenger (peace be upon him) supplicated with it in the Battle of Badr. And this wording is well-known in those hadiths. (S). (1) So He glorified hears and sees in pre-eternity His high essence and all His existential attributes, including His hearing and His sight, and He hears and sees forever the essences of all contingent things and all their existential attributes, however each of them may be. So His hearing and sight are not conditioned by extreme distance or extreme speed, whereas our sight ordinarily only relates to some existents, namely bodies and their colors, motion, and rest, conditioned that the seen be in the front direction and not be too far nor too close. (G). And this is because His hearing is an attribute of His attributes, not a limb of Him as the corporealists imagine, for they say that God has two eyes and that each eye of them is pointed to by a pointing different from the other, and that one of them is to the right of the other. This is pure corporealism, exalted is God above it, and it is among the fabrications of the corporealists. As for us, we say: just as God has an attribute which is knowledge, He also has an attribute which is hearing, and His hearing is without limb or organ, as is the case with the creature, and likewise is said concerning His sight. (S). The Sunnah: His statement (peace be upon him) when he passed by people asking for rain and supplicating to God aloud, he said: 'O people, be gentle with yourselves - i.e., give yourselves respite - for you are not calling upon a deaf or blind one, but rather you are calling upon an All-Hearing, All-Seeing One.' (1) And the community has agreed that God is All-Hearing, All-Seeing, and the rational proof will come. Note: Know that He hears with His hearing by His hearing and sees with His sight by His sight, just as He knows with His knowledge by His knowledge, because the attributes of disclosure relate to themselves, unlike the attributes of effect, for they relate only to possibles.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the divine attributes of hearing (sam') and sight (baṣr). The author begins by defining each as an eternal attribute by which every existent is disclosed to God, emphasizing that the disclosure of hearing is distinct from that of sight. They are two attributes, confirmed by revelation and obligatory to believe in. They do not add to God's knowledge in terms of disclosure, but differ in their specific reality and relation to existents, whether eternal (like God's essence and attributes) or originated (like contingent beings). The relation to God's essence and attributes is an eternal active relation (tanjīzī qadīm), while to contingent beings it is an originated active relation (tanjīzī ḥādith) and an eternal potential relation (ṣulūḥī qadīm). Then the author provides scriptural proof: from the Qur'an, the verse 'And He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing'; and from the Sunnah, several hadiths including the one about the greatest name of God and the hadith 'You are not calling upon a deaf or blind one.' The author clarifies that divine hearing and sight are not conditioned by physical factors like distance or speed, unlike human sight which has conditions. Then comes a refutation of anthropomorphism (tajsīm): the author rejects the view of the corporealists (mujassimah) who say God has eyes as limbs, stating that this is pure corporealism and a fabrication. Instead, the Ahl al-Sunnah affirm hearing and sight as attributes without organs. The passage concludes with a note that the attributes of disclosure (hearing, sight, knowledge) relate to themselves (i.e., they are self-referential in their disclosure), unlike attributes of effect (like power and will) which relate only to possibles. The rational proof is promised later.

Key Terms

بصر
صفة أزلية
انكشاف
تنجيزي
صلوحي

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relation of hearing and sight to existents that are originated (like contingent beings)?
A) An eternal active relation only.
B) An originated active relation and an eternal potential relation.
C) An eternal potential relation only.
D) No relation at all.

Key Takeaway
Hearing and sight are distinct eternal attributes that disclose all existents, with a specific relation to contingent beings that combines originated actuality and eternal potentiality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that God's hearing discloses every existing thing—not just sounds but your innermost thoughts—do you still act as if you can hide something from Him? What one habit of secrecy will you let go of after this lesson?
?
The author says hearing and sight do not add to God's knowledge but are distinct attributes. Does your daily life reflect a belief that God knows, hears, and sees your every action with equal clarity? If not, what specific moment today will you remind yourself of this truth?
?
God's sight has an eternal relation to His essence and an originated active relation to your deeds. Are you treating your actions as if they only matter in this world, or do you truly believe that at each instant His sight creates a new relation to you? What will you do differently in your next prayer to align with this reality?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
8 min
Scriptural Proofs and Refuting Anthropomorphism
Provides scriptural proofs and refutes anthropomorphism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence for hearing and sight as divine attributes and the refutation of the anthropomorphic view that God has physical organs.

Core Idea
Scripture proves God hears and sees, but without limbs; anthropomorphism is a fabrication.

Having defined the attributes, Sanusi now provides scriptural proofs: a Qur’anic verse and several hadiths. He then clarifies that divine hearing and sight are not conditioned by physical factors like distance or speed, unlike human perception. The passage concludes with a strong refutation of the corporealists (mujassimah) who attribute eyes and limbs to God, affirming that hearing and sight are attributes without organs.

Guided Path
1
Examine the Qur’anic proof
Read the verse 'And He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing' and the accompanying hadith about the greatest name. Note that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used this supplication frequently.
The verse is a direct proof that God has these attributes.
2
Study the hadith evidence
Consider the hadith 'You are not calling upon a deaf or blind one'—it affirms that God hears and sees. Also note the mention of community consensus (ijma‘).
The sunnah reinforces the Qur’an.
3
Understand the conditions of perception
The passage contrasts divine hearing/sight with human senses: human sight requires certain conditions (front direction, moderate distance, etc.), whereas God’s attributes are unconditioned.
This avoids limiting God by physical constraints.
4
Refute anthropomorphism
Read the refutation of the mujassimah who claim God has eyes as limbs. The author declares this pure corporealism and a fabrication, affirming that hearing and sight are attributes without body parts.
This clarifies the Sunni position against tashbih.

Misconception: Some people believe that God's hearing and sight are similar to human senses, implying physical organs like ears and eyes.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between divine hearing/sight and human perception?
A) Divine hearing/sight are conditioned by distance and speed, while human perception is not.

?

?

The Nature of Divine Speech (Al-Kalam)
Definition of divine speech with two negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine speech is an eternal meaning subsisting in God's essence, not composed of letters or sounds like human speech.

Core Idea
God's speech is a timeless meaning, not letters or sounds.

A common mistake is to imagine God's speech as similar to human speech, composed of words and sounds. In this passage, Sanusi clarifies the true nature of divine speech: it is an eternal attribute, a meaning that subsists in God's essence, free from the limitations of created language. Let's read his definition carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation to get the gist.
Notice that the Arabic cuts off; the argument is complete for our purpose.
2
Identify the definition of speech
The author defines the reality of speech as 'the meaning subsisting in the essence.' Mark this phrase and consider what it implies about divine speech.
This is the positive statement.
3
Note the negations: not letters, not sounds
The author explicitly denies that God's speech is composed of letters or sounds, because they are created (ḥāditha). Understand why this follows from the definition.
These are the two negative statements.
4
Reflect on the implications
Contrast this with human speech. How does this understanding protect God's transcendence?
This reinforces the Ashʿarī position that divine attributes are eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام وحقيقة الكلام هو المعنى القائم بالذات المعبر عنه بالعبارات المختلفات المباين الجنس الحروف والأصوات المنزه عن التقديم والتأخير والكل والبعض واللحن والإعراب وسائر أنواع التغيرات المتعلق بما يتعلق به العلم من المتعلقات. وكلام الله تعالى ليس بحروف لأن الحروف حادثة. وكلام الله ليس بصوت لأن الأصوات حادثة ، والحروف والأصوات فيهما
Speech: The reality of speech is the meaning subsisting in the essence, expressed by different expressions, being different in kind from letters and sounds, transcendent of prefixing and postponing, of whole and part, of solecism and inflection and all types of changes, related to that which knowledge relates to from among the relata. And the speech of God is not composed of letters, because letters are originated. And the speech of God is not sound, because sounds are originated, and letters and sounds in them
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a definition of divine speech (al-kalām). The author states that the reality of speech is a meaning (ma'nā) that subsists in the essence (al-dhāt) of God, expressed by various expressions, but it is different in kind from letters and sounds. This meaning is transcendent of temporal sequence (like prefixing and postponing), of division (whole and part), and of linguistic errors (solecism, inflection) and all types of changes. It is related to the same objects that knowledge is related to. Then the author makes two negative statements: (1) God's speech is not composed of letters, because letters are originated (ḥāditha); (2) God's speech is not sound, because sounds are originated. The passage cuts off after mentioning 'letters and sounds in them', likely continuing to explain that both are created but speech is not. This affirms the Ash'ari position that divine speech is an eternal attribute of the essence, not a temporal creation.

Allah's Attributes of Hearing and Sight
Sanusi cites a hadith and notes that Allah is Sami' Basir with specific attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes of hearing and sight are established by the Sunnah and consensus, and that they are intrinsic attributes of disclosure, not dependent on creation.

Core Idea
Allah hears and sees without need for ears or eyes.

In this lesson, we examine the proof from the Sunnah and the consensus of the Ummah that Allah is Hearing and Seeing. The Prophet's hadith teaches us that Allah hears and sees us directly. The passage also clarifies the nature of these attributes as 'attributes of disclosure' intrinsic to Allah, unlike attributes of effect that relate to creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the hadith cited by the Prophet (PBUH) and notice its context: people calling loudly for rain, and the Prophet instructing them to be gentle because they are not calling upon a deaf or blind deity.
The hadith emphasizes that Allah hears and sees directly, without any intermediary.
2
Understand the consensus
Note that the Ummah has unanimously agreed that Allah is Sami' (Hearing) and Basir (Seeing). This consensus is a secondary proof after the Sunnah.
Consensus (ijma') is a source of Islamic law and theology.
3
Distinguish attribute types
Read the note carefully: attributes of disclosure (ṣifāt al-inkishāf) like hearing, sight, and knowledge relate to themselves—they are inherent in Allah. Attributes of effect (ṣifāt al-ta'thīr) like creating relate to possible things.
This distinction shows that Allah's hearing and sight do not depend on creation.
4
Reflect on the meaning
Ask yourself: Why does this distinction matter? It guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih) and affirms that Allah's attributes are real yet unlike creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السنة قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لما مرَّ بأناس يستسقون ويدعون الله جهراً فقال : 'يا أيها الناس أربعوا على أنفسكم - أي أمهلوا عليها - فإنكم لم تدعوا أصم ولا أعمى وإنما تدعون سميعاً بصيراً'. وأجمعت الأمة على أن الله تعالى سميع بصير، ودليل العقل فسيأتي. ملاحظة : اعلم أنه تعالى يسمع سمعه بسمعه ويبصر بصره ببصره كما أنه يعلم علمه بعلمه، لأن صفات الانكشاف تتعلق بأنفسها بخلاف صفات التأثير فإنها تتعلق بالممكنات فقط.
The Sunnah: His saying, peace be upon him, when he passed by people asking for rain and calling upon Allah loudly, he said: 'O people, be gentle with yourselves - i.e., give yourselves respite - for you are not calling upon a deaf or blind one, but you are calling upon a Hearing, Seeing (One).' And the Ummah has agreed that Allah is Hearing, Seeing, and the intellectual proof will come later. Note: Know that He hears with His hearing and sees with His sight, just as He knows with His knowledge, because the attributes of disclosure (ṣifāt al-inkishāf) are related to themselves, unlike the attributes of effect (ṣifāt al-ta'thīr), which are related only to possible things.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents the proof from the Sunnah and consensus for Allah's attributes of hearing and sight. It begins by citing a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) tells people that they are not calling upon a deaf or blind deity, but upon one who hears and sees. This establishes that hearing and sight are real attributes of Allah. Then it notes that the Muslim Ummah is in consensus that Allah is Hearing and Seeing, and mentions that the intellectual proof will be given later. The passage adds an important note: Allah hears with His hearing and sees with His sight, just as He knows with His knowledge. This is because attributes of disclosure (like hearing, sight, knowledge, and will) are related to themselves—that is, they are inherent in the divine essence. In contrast, attributes of effect (like creating and providing) are related only to possible things. This distinction highlights that hearing and sight are not dependent on created objects; they are intrinsic to the divine nature.

God's Speech is Not Letters or Sounds: Refutation of Anthropomorphic Views
Refutation of views that God's speech is letters or sounds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunnah affirms that God's speech is an eternal attribute not composed of letters or sounds, and recognize the flaws in opposing views.

Core Idea
God's speech is not letters or sounds; it is an eternal mental attribute.

This passage defends the Ash'ari doctrine that God's speech (kalām nafsī) is an eternal attribute, distinct from created letters and sounds. The author refutes three erroneous views: that speech is eternal letters/sounds (al-'Aḍud), that it is letters/sounds relative to attribution (some Ḥanābilā), and that it is contingent letters/sounds created in God's essence (Ibn Taymiyya). By examining these refutations, we grasp why anthropomorphic analogies fail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the opening statement: God's speech transcends precedence, posteriority, secrecy, and loudness. Note that the annotation (1) explicitly says it is not a letter or sound, which is the relied-upon view of Ahl al-Sunnah.
This is the thesis of the passage.
2
Examine the three refuted views
The passage refutes three positions: 1) al-'Aḍud's eternal letters and sounds, 2) the Ḥanābila's relative eternity/contingency, 3) the Ḥashwiyya's contingent letters created in God's essence. For each, note the author's objection.
Pay attention to the logical flaws highlighted.
3
Understand the argument from inner speech
The author uses the example of a child's inner speech to show that 'kalām' in language includes mental speech, which precedes vocal speech. This undermines the necessity of letters and sounds.
Inner speech is a condition for vocal speech, not dependent on it.
4
Reflect on the invalidity of analogy
The opponents' analogy of Creator to creature is declared 'falsest of falsehoods'. Consider why reasoning from human speech to divine speech is invalid.
The passage also notes that vocal speech would imply gradual acquisition of perfection in God, which is impossible.

تقديم وتأخير وكلام الله تعالى منزه عن ذلك (۱) ، وليس بسر أيضاً ولا جهر لأنهما من كلام الحوادث. (1) كون كلام الله تعالى ليس بحرف ولا بصوت هو المعتمد عند أهل السنة بل هو الحق الذي لا ريب فيه ، وقال العضد إنه بحروف وأصوات قديمة ويلزم عليه كما قال المتأخرون أن كلامه تعالى فيه التقدم والتأخر، لكن أجيب عن ذلك : بأن حروفنا إنما جاءها التقدم والتأخر من اختلاف المخارج، ومن تنزه عن ذلك تنزه كلامه عن ذلك، وهذا الكلام إنما سرى للعضد من الحشوية فلا يعوّل عليه. وقال جماعة نسبوا أنفسهم إلى الحنابلة إنه بحروف وأصوات لكن إن نسبت إليه تعالى كانت قديمة، وإن نسبت إلى الحوادث كانت حادثة ، ولا يخفى بطلان هذا الكلام (ج ) ولا يخفى أن كلام العضد ضعيف وقد نبه على ذلك الإمام السعد في شرح العقائد النسفية، ووضح الشريف الجرجاني حاصل رأي العضد هذا في شرح المواقف، وقد ذكر هناك أن العضد ذكر رأيه هذا في مقالة خاصة في الكلام فتأمل. ولكن إذا كان العضد يقصد بذلك ما وقع في علم الله تعالى فله وجه، مع أنه غير محل الخلاف. واعلم أن بعض الحشوية الذين انتسبوا إلى السلف الصالح وهم منهم براء، ادعوا أن كلام الله تعالى عبارة عن حوادث هي حروف وأصوات تقوم هذه الحروف والأصوات بذاته الشريفة، وتكون تابعة لإرادته وقدرته أي إن الله تعالى يوجدها في ذاته بعد أن لم تكن موجودة، وهي حادثة الشخص قديمة النوع ، أي إن كل كلمة منها حادثة، وأما جنس الكلام فهو قديم، لأن الله يتكلم إذا شاء، ومشيئته تعالى قديمة، فيلزم عليه أن يكون كلامه قديماً بالنوع حادثاً بالأفراد. وهذا هو حقيقة قول ابن تيمية ومن تبعه وقد صرح به في أكثر من موضع. واعلم أن هذا المذهب باطل، ولا دليل عليه من الكتاب والسنة، ولكنهم جروا في ذلك على قياس كلام الخالق على كلام المخلوق، فقالوا إن كل كلام نراه في الشاهد فهو بحرف وصوت، فبما أنه قد ثبت أن الله متكلم فيجب إذن أن يكون كلامه بحرف وصوت. وظاهر أن هذا قياس للخالق على المخلوق، وهو من أبطل الباطل. فلا يلزم إذا كان كلام المخلوق حرفاً وصوتاً أن يكون كلام الله تعالى كذلك. ثم إننا نعلم أن الكلام في اللغة قد يطلق على الإشارات والعقد بالأصابع وعلى الكلام النفسي الذي يشعر به كل إنسان في نفسه. فالطفل الصغير قبل أن يتحدث بحرف وصوت فإنه يكون قبل ذلك يحدث نفسه بالكلام النفسي، فالكلام النفسي سابق في الوجود على الكلام بالحرف والصوت، بل هو شرط وجود الكلام الذي بالحرف والصوت، يعلم ذلك من لاحظ الطفل وهو يتعلم الكلام، والتفصيل في الاستدلال على الكلام النفسي ليس هذا محله، فقياسهم إذن معتمد على مقدمة باطلة، مع أن الكلام اللفظي يلزم عليه النقص للذات واستكمال الذات لكمالاتها على التدريج، وهو باطل بلا توقف.(س).
Precedence and posteriority: and the speech of God, exalted, is transcendent of that (1), and it is not secret nor loud because they are from the speech of contingent beings. (1) That the speech of God, exalted, is not a letter nor a sound is what is relied upon by the People of the Sunnah, rather it is the truth about which there is no doubt. Al-‘Aḍud said that it consists of letters and sounds that are eternal, and it follows, as the later scholars said, that His speech, exalted, contains precedence and posteriority. But that was answered: that our letters acquire precedence and posteriority only from the difference of articulation points, and He who transcends that, His speech transcends that. This view only reached al-‘Aḍud from the Ḥashwiyya, so it is not to be relied upon. A group who attributed themselves to the Ḥanābila said that it consists of letters and sounds, but if attributed to Him, exalted, they are eternal, and if attributed to contingent beings, they are contingent. The invalidity of this statement is not hidden. (j) It is not hidden that the statement of al-‘Aḍud is weak, and Imām al-Sa‘d pointed that out in his commentary on al-‘Aqā’id al-Nasafiyya, and al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī clarified the gist of al-‘Aḍud’s opinion in Sharḥ al-Mawāqif. He mentioned there that al-‘Aḍud presented this opinion in a special treatise on speech, so reflect. But if al-‘Aḍud intended by that what occurs in God’s knowledge, then it has a face, though it is not the subject of dispute. Know that some of the Ḥashwiyya who claimed association with the righteous predecessors (al-salaf al-ṣāliḥ) but are innocent of them, claimed that God’s speech, exalted, consists of contingencies that are letters and sounds that subsist in His noble essence, subject to His will and power—that is, God, exalted, brings them into existence in His essence after they were not existent. They are contingent as individuals, eternal as species; that is, each word of them is contingent, but the genus of speech is eternal, because God speaks when He wills, and His will, exalted, is eternal. Consequently, His speech would be eternal as species, contingent as individuals. This is the reality of the statement of Ibn Taymiyya and those who follow him, and he stated it explicitly in more than one place. Know that this madhhab is false, and there is no evidence for it from the Book and Sunnah. Rather, they proceeded in that by analogy of the speech of the Creator to the speech of the creature, saying: every speech we see in the witnessed world is by letter and sound, so since it has been established that God speaks, then necessarily His speech must be by letter and sound. Evidently, this is an analogy of the Creator to the creature, and it is among the falsest of falsehoods. It does not follow that if the speech of the creature is letter and sound, then God’s speech, exalted, must be likewise. Moreover, we know that speech in language may be applied to gestures and signs with fingers, and to inner speech (al-kalām al-nafsī) which every human feels in himself. A small child before he speaks with letter and sound, before that he talks to himself with inner speech. So inner speech precedes in existence the speech that uses letter and sound, rather it is a condition for the existence of speech that uses letter and sound. This is known by observing a child learning to speak. Detailing the proof for inner speech is not its place here. So their analogy is founded on a false premise, besides that vocal speech would entail deficiency for the essence and the essence's acquisition of its perfections gradually, which is false without hesitation. (s)
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument asserting that God's speech (kalām Allāh) is not composed of letters or sounds, and refuting contrary views. The author begins by stating that God's speech transcends precedence, posteriority, secrecy, or loudness, as these pertain to contingent speech. In the annotation (1), he affirms the Ash‘arī consensus that God's speech is not a letter or a sound. He then refutes al-‘Aḍud's claim that speech consists of eternal letters and sounds, noting that this leads to temporal sequence in the divine essence—an impossibility. The author traces this error to the Ḥashwiyya and dismisses it. Next, he refutes a group claiming to be Ḥanābilā who say speech is letters and sounds but relative: eternal when attributed to God, contingent otherwise. He declares this invalid. He then criticizes al-‘Aḍud's position as weak, citing that al-Sa‘d al-Taftāzānī and al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī have exposed its flaws, yet allows a charitable interpretation if al-‘Aḍud meant knowledge in God's mind. The author then addresses the Ḥashwiyya—those claiming to follow the Salaf—who assert that God's speech consists of contingent letters and sounds subsisting in His essence, created by His will and power. They hold that each individual speech event is contingent but the genus is eternal. The author identifies this as Ibn Taymiyya's position. He declares it baseless, lacking scriptural evidence, and rooted in an anthropomorphic analogy (qiyās) between Creator and creature. He further argues that the Arabic term 'kalām' has broader meanings, including inner speech (al-kalām al-nafsī), which is a pre-linguistic mental reality. The fact that a child possesses inner speech before articulate sounds shows that vocal speech is not essential. Thus the opponent's analogy fails. Moreover, vocal speech would imply that God acquires perfections gradually, which is impossible for the Necessary Being. The passage concludes that the view attributing letters and sounds to God is definitively false.

Key Terms
كلام الله
الحروف والأصوات
الكلام النفسي
القياس
الحشوية
ابن تيمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because human speech uses letters and sounds, God's speech must also be letters and sounds.
Correction: This is an anthropomorphic analogy. God's speech is an eternal attribute unlike created speech. The Arabic word 'kalām' includes inner speech, which is not dependent on letters/sounds.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view of God's speech?
A) It consists of eternal letters and sounds.
B) It is an eternal attribute not composed of letters or sounds.
C) It is letters and sounds that are contingent when attributed to God.
D) It is inner speech only, without any external expression.

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters or sounds; anthropomorphic analogy and any view implying contingency or temporality in God's essence are false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself visually imagining God speaking to you in a human voice or with an accent? How does this lesson challenge that mental image, and what concrete step will you take today to replace it with the correct understanding of God's eternal, non-articulate speech?

?
This lesson warns against the fallacy of comparing the Creator to the creature. In which hidden corners of your theology (e.g., your understanding of God's anger, His mercy, His seeing, or His hearing) might you be unconsciously slipping into the same error? Why Revealed Scriptures Are Called God's Speech
Explains the derivative naming of revealed scriptures as God's speech and their relation to the eternal attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the revealed scriptures (Torah, Gospel, Qur'an) are called God's speech in a derivative sense, and how they relate to the eternal attribute of inner speech.

Core Idea
Revealed books are God's speech by indication, not identity.

We often refer to the Qur'an, Torah, and Gospel as God's speech. But what exactly does that mean? Are these books identical to God's eternal attribute of speech, or is there a distinction? In this passage, the author clarifies that the scriptures are called God's speech in a derivative sense: they either indicate the eternal inner speech or are created by God, but they are not the attribute itself. Understanding this distinction prevents theological errors about God's attributes and the nature of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the key distinction
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to how the author distinguishes between the revealed words and the eternal inner speech (al-kalām al-nafsī).
Look for phrases like 'ليست هي نفس الصفة النفسية'.
2
Understand the basis for calling scriptures God's speech
Identify the two main reasons given: (1) they indicate the inner speech, and (2) God created them. Both are derivative uses of the term 'speech of God'.
The annotation (2) elaborates on these reasons.
3
Grasp the warning about language
Notice the caution against saying 'the speech of God is created' or 'the Qur'an is created' because of possible confusion with the eternal attribute. The author explains when it is permissible.
This is in annotation (1).
4
Reflect on the scope of revealed knowledge
Consider that the inner speech contains infinite knowledge, while the scriptures convey only a portion. This explains why there are different scriptures in different languages.
Annotation (3) makes this point.
